﻿Soulpulse Resonance Magic System (Confluence Chronicles)
Metaphysical Foundations of Soulpulse
Vibrational Resonance Energy: Soulpulse is the innate magic of Te’Oga, operating on principles of resonance and vibration rather than brute force. It flows through an invisible planetary vein-network like currents in a living organism[1][2]. Every structure, element, and living being has a natural frequency – a unique vibrational signature – and each practitioner’s soul has its own “pulse” frequency[3][4]. Magic occurs not by imposing will, but by matching frequencies: when a Soulpulse user attunes their inner vibration to an external target’s frequency, a sympathetic resonance arises and reality shifts smoothly in response[5][6]. This is why early users described it not as commanding matter, but “coaxing the world to sing along” – a poetic truth that hides a rigorous principle.
Resonance Friction and Vein-Burn: If the frequencies clash instead of harmonizing, the result is resonance friction – the magical equivalent of grinding gears. In practical terms, failed Soulpulse attempts produce dissonance: harsh vibrational clashes that can shatter materials, backfire on the user, and scorch their internal “veins”[7]. Practitioners experience this as vein-burn, an internal burning pain and damage to their channels. For example, in the first known Soulpulse usage, Jhace Torrins desperately attuned to metal and flesh to save a friend; he succeeded, but his forearm veins glowed copper-gold and burned from within as mismatched resonance energy seared him[8]. Vein-burn is the heat of friction between soul-frequency and world-frequency – a literal cost paid in pain and injury when one’s will “rubs raw” against reality. Over time, repeated minor vein-burn accumulates as scars or tremors, while severe dissonance can cripple a practitioner on the spot.
Divine Opposition of Principles: At the heart of Soulpulse theory are four fundamental resonance principles that seem to underlie all magical effects: Form, Purity, Wholeness, and Entropy. These can be thought of as four great musical tones or cosmic currents, each with a distinct nature and intrinsically opposed counterpart. Form (structure/order) stands opposite to Entropy (dissolution/ending), while Purity (cleansing/separation) stands opposite to Wholeness (healing/connection). Metaphysically, each principle generates a unique “field” of influence and a set of frequencies, and when one principle is invoked, its opposite resists like a countermelody. This divine opposition means no creation of perfect order can occur without stirring entropy, and no act of total inclusion can occur without provoking some force of exclusion. Practically, a Soulpulse user aligned strongly to one principle finds it hardest to wield or withstand its opposite – an important limitation built into the magic’s fabric.
Pulse-Field Dynamics: Using Soulpulse creates a pulse-field, a vibrational aura that extends beyond the body into nearby matter and even other practitioners. These fields interact in complex ways. When harmonized (e.g. two healers working together in sync), they amplify each other, producing effects far greater than either could alone[9]. When disparate frequencies collide, they create interference or outright feedback loops. Unintended feedback can lead to a Resonance Cascade, where energy jumps unpredictably through the environment: one poorly tuned pulse might trigger vibrations in adjacent structures or in the planetary veins underfoot, causing chain reactions like collapsing buildings or “pulse-quakes” in the land[10]. The planet’s vein-network itself carries large-scale pulse-fields; after the catastrophic Piercing event, Te’Oga’s entire crust hummed with a new vibration, and when a massive global resonance was later triggered, it caused reality to oscillate violently (the Fathom Break). In essence, Soulpulse obeys physics-like laws of wave interference – constructive and destructive interference, propagation through mediums – giving it a rigorous logic even at its most fantastical. Masters of the art study pulse-field dynamics the way engineers study pressure systems, learning how energy distributes through materials and how far a change will ripple before dissipating.
Mechanics of Soulpulse: Attunement, Overtone, and Dissonance
Resonance Matching & Attunement: To produce a magical effect, a practitioner must attune to their target. This involves sensing or guessing the target’s natural frequency and gradually adjusting one’s Soulpulse output to match[11]. It is a subtle art akin to tuning a musical instrument or finding the right key in which to hum. In practice, the user focuses will, emotion, and often a precise gesture or tool, sending out a probing pulse. If the frequency aligns, resonance is achieved – metal strengthens or bends, wounds knit closed, toxins purge, flames spark, etc., depending on the intent and principle[8][6]. If the frequency is off by even a little, the user feels resistance – a dissonant feedback in their bones – warning them to adjust. Experienced Soulpulsers describe a tactile sensation when they're close to attunement: the world feels pliable, like a note on the verge of ringing true. By contrast, pushing ahead without attuning is like trying to force the wrong key into a lock: the magic “jams” and often backfires with pain or destructive consequences.
Attunement is easiest when one is patient and perceptive. “Don’t push. Invite. Glass will tell you when it’s ready,” as master glassmith Tiffani often instructs[12]. Her glass-working approach epitomizes attunement – gently heating and waiting for the material to respond – whereas a forge-trained smith might initially try to hammer change into the world. This difference played out when Tiffani taught Jhace: by measuring, listening, and guiding rather than brute-forcing, he found the broken glass and metal around him resonated and mended far better[13][14]. The lesson: Soulpulse isn’t raw force at all, but cooperative resonance[15]. Attunement can sometimes require multiple attempts or creative approaches – sensing temperature changes, audible hums, or emotional tone of a target – but once locked in, the effect feels almost effortless, as if the world itself completes the work.
Overtone Theory & Multi-Resonance: While most practitioners have one predominant resonance (their affinity principle), advanced Soulpulse use involves overtones – secondary frequencies that a user can layer atop their fundamental tone. In music, plucking a string produces not just one note but a series of harmonics; analogously, a skilled resonator might introduce a second principle as a harmonious overtone to their primary principle. This is exceedingly difficult and was long thought impossible beyond minor tricks. However, cases of dual-principle mastery proved overtones can be harnessed: Jhace himself instinctively used multiple resonance types in quick succession under battle duress[16], and Tiffani later deliberately combined Form + Wholeness resonance in a single act to perform an “impossible” healing[17][18]. They achieved a resonant chord, so to speak, balancing two frequencies in harmony. Overtone theory posits that all four principles are ultimately facets of one grand spectrum – meaning, in theory, a being could resonate with every principle at once if their soul could handle the complexity. This ultimate multi-resonance is called Confluence (all principles in simultaneous focus)[19]. It was only witnessed once – a desperate Jhace, in grief, unconsciously harmonized Form, Purity, Wholeness, and Entropy together, unleashing an unfathomably powerful omni-resonant pulse[20][21]. Overtone magic is powerful but perilous: the more principles intertwined, the more unstable the combined frequency. Even dual resonance puts extreme strain on body and mind (Tiffani’s vein-burn scar accelerated when she channeled two principles[22]). Only a unique soul or extraordinary circumstances can sustain a full Confluence without shattering.
Pulse-Field Feedback: Resonant energy tends to linger briefly as an echo in whatever medium was affected. After a Soulpulse action, the practitioner and environment carry residual vibrations – akin to a ringing that slowly fades. If one tries to use Soulpulse again immediately, these vein-echoes can interfere with the new attempt[23]. This phenomenon, known colloquially as echo stacking, can amplify errors: imagine trying to sing a new note while the old note’s echo still reverberates, causing discord. Practitioners must learn to either wait for the echo to dissipate or deliberately dampen it (through meditation or grounding techniques) before attempting another major pulse. Failure to do so often results in a jarring dissonance spike and severe vein-burn as the leftover vibrations clash with the new ones[24]. In group settings, pulse-field feedback is an even greater concern – multiple people working at near frequencies can accidentally create a resonant feedback loop. Teams of Continuity resonators (healers) learned this when too many tried to heal one patient simultaneously: their well-intentioned overlapping pulses caused a painful thrumming in the patient and themselves. Conversely, a team that staggers their efforts or harmonizes precisely can amplify effects safely (this disciplined coordination is what made grand construction projects possible in Prism – dozens of Form resonators all singing the same note, so to speak). Feedback loops are thus both a hazard and a tool – uncontrolled, they lead to Resonance Cascades and disasters; controlled, they lead to symphonies of power.
Dissonance and Failure Modes: When attunement fails, the results are immediate and often dramatic. Minor dissonance produces a harsh buzz of pain in the user’s veins and aborts the effect, often leaving a scorch mark on the user’s skin or the target object as a warning. Severe dissonance – actively clashing frequency output – causes immediate vein-burn and can even Vein-Snap the user’s internal channels[25]. A vein-snap is a metaphysical rupture analogous to a torn muscle: the practitioner might collapse, coughing blood or losing feeling in a limb as their soul-circuits temporarily shut down[25]. The environment doesn’t escape unscathed either; strong dissonance can shatter nearby glass, splinter wood, or buckle metal as the “wrong note” violently disagrees with reality[26][7]. One notable incident involved a young multi-resonant, Chloen, who attempted an advanced structural pulse she wasn’t attuned for – her arm and a nearby worker’s veins snapped from the backlash, and support beams around them fractured[27]. Such failures taught early practitioners hard limits.
Beyond immediate failures, there are cascading failures: if a resonator stubbornly pushes through dissonance, each subsequent attempt becomes more erratic as both user and target fall out of tune. In worst cases this leads to a Resonance Cascade (uncontrolled chain reaction) or even psychological break (extreme dissonance can flood the mind with static, inducing temporary madness or unconsciousness). Thus, a core law of Soulpulse emerged: the magic will “fight back” if forced. It is a dialogue, not a monologue. The more a user insists without listening, the more the resulting dissonance punishes them. This principle enforced humility and caution among those who might otherwise abuse such power.
The Four Divine Principles: Form, Purity, Wholeness, Entropy
In time, all Soulpulse abilities were understood to fall under one (or a combination) of Four Resonance Principles, which later gained near-mythic status as divine aspects. Each principle has distinct effects, costs, personality tendencies, and even drew its own following and cultural worship once their true power was revealed. Below is an in-depth look at each:
Form – The Principle of Structure and Order (Structural Resonance)
Essence & Effects: Form resonance embodies rigidity, structure, and ideal shape. Its frequency is described as high and crystalline, a sharp clarion ring that brings stillness and strength[28]. Form resonators can reinforce physical structures, impose geometric order on chaos, and “lock” objects or systems into their optimal configuration[28]. In practical use, this ranges from strengthening a collapsing building by infusing it with rigid energy, to straightening a bent metal beam, to creating barriers of force that hold fast. At its extremes, Form resonance can even crystallize fluids or mend shattered glass into seamless, symmetric patterns. The guiding intention is perfection – making things conform to an ideal blueprint.
Metaphysical Role: Form is often seen as the cosmic force of law and stability. It resists change and decay, seeking everlasting order. Its divine opposite is Entropy – whenever a Form user tries to preserve or create structure, entropy subtly works to unravel it over time. These two principles are in eternal tension, much like order vs chaos. Practically, a strong Form effect (say, magically reinforcing a fortress wall) will hold for long, but natural entropy will make it require periodic renewal, and a Dissolution adept might more easily undo another’s Form-work. Form is the skeleton of reality, giving shape to existence.
Costs & Limitations: The mantra of Form is “rigidity at a price.” Form practitioners gradually pay with their flexibility – both physical and mental. Prolonged use causes the user’s joints to stiffen and muscles to calcify[29]; many veteran Structuralists suffer from chronic pain or limited range of motion, as if their bodies are turning into the stone and metal they often reinforce. Symbolically, they risk becoming rigid in mind as well: an adherence to rules and perfectionism that can border on obsession. Early on, Corlexi (a gifted Form resonator) exemplified this cost – his fixation on geometric perfection and refusal to accept “good enough” were personality traits amplified by his resonance[30][31]. The physical toll was evident in practitioners who overused Form: calcified growths on bones, a literal ossification caused by channeling so much rigid energy. If pushed too far, Form users can experience Hollowing (detailed later) when their conviction in creating order collapses under impossible standards[32].
Personality & Traits: Those attuned to Form tend to be methodical, precise, and control-focused[33]. They often have engineering or architectural mindsets, seeing structures and systems in everything. Many were drawn from (or became) the Structuralist faction, known for bureaucracy and enforcing standards. Culturally, Structuralists (pejoratively called “The Rigid”) valued order above all – they instituted licensing for magic use to maintain control[34], and wore blue-silver insignia reflecting the crystalline blue-silver glow their Soulpulse emits in use[28]. The Form principle appeals to those who fear chaos; in the post-Piercing world of Te’Oga, many clung to Form as a way to rebuild and feel safe through rules and structure.
Worship & Mythos: After the Fathom Break, Form literally ascended in the figure of Xilcore, the God of Form (formerly Corlexi). In a blinding moment, Corlexi’s body restructured into a state of geometric perfection – he became a living avatar of law and structure[35]. Followers, including former Structuralists, proclaimed him the “God of Law”, seeing the hand of destiny in his transformation[36]. Entire swathes of survivors began worshiping Form in a religious sense – praying for stability and protection under Xilcore. The cultural image of Form thus shifted from a mere magical affinity to a divine principle of order: cities under Xilcore’s influence started to rebuild in grand symmetry, and draconian codes were enforced as though sins against structural perfection were sacrilege. The Personality of Form as a divine principle became dogmatic, unyielding, yet reassuring to those who craved certainty. Even before this apotheosis, temples and guild-halls had iconography of the “Great Builder” or “Architect” – concepts now understood to have been foreshadowing the coming of a Form deity. Yet even worshipers acknowledge the double-edged nature of this power: Form promises peace through order, but taken too far it can be tyrannical (crystal that traps life in static perfection). Culturally, Form’s rise caused friction with those who value freedom or change, setting the stage for ideological conflict with Entropy’s followers especially.
Purity – The Principle of Cleansing and Isolation (Purification Resonance)
Essence & Effects: Purity resonance revolves around separation, refinement, and absolution. It seeks to remove that which “does not belong” – whether physical impurities in materials, illness in a body, or even moral “corruption” in a system. Its frequency is often described as a clear, piercing tone with a singular focus, like a bell that cuts through noise. Purity resonators can cleanse water or food of toxins effortlessly, draw out poison or disease from a person, and purify metals or gems to an immaculate state. In combat or aggressive use, the same power becomes frightening: a Purity user can literally burn away whatever they deem impure. This might manifest as white-hot Soulpulse flames that incinerate impurities (for instance, burning out infection from flesh – or burning a living being whom the user sees as “impure”). One Purity adept, Mobel, in a duel pulled the impurities out of Jhace’s body – an agonizing technique that nearly tore him apart from within[37]. Purity’s positive side is holy and healing in appearance (removing only what shouldn’t be there), but in zealot hands it becomes a weapon of judgment, sparing nothing but an imagined perfect core.
Metaphysical Role: Purity serves as the cosmic filter. It is the force that divides light from darkness, the meaningful from the meaningless, striving for an unattainable absolute perfection. Its opposite principle is Wholeness (Continuity). Where Wholeness seeks to join and heal regardless of imperfections, Purity insists that only by excising the flawed can true integrity be achieved. These philosophies are fundamentally at odds: one inclusive, one exclusive. On a cosmic scale, Purity can be thought of as the principle of singularity – narrowing the world down to a single truth or essence by eliminating all else. This makes it a dangerously absolute power, one that doesn’t lend itself to balance. Unsurprisingly, it was the least understood (and most feared) of the four principles until late in the Chronicles; it hid in the shadows, quietly intensifying in isolated pockets (like remote temples) until it exploded onto the world stage.
Costs & Limitations: The pursuit of purity is inherently a path of sacrifice and self-harm. Those who channel Purity frequently experience the need to sacrifice parts of themselves – metaphorically and literally. Physically, Purity resonance tends to manifest as searing heat or caustic energy through the user’s veins. Practitioners often exhibit inflammation, cracked skin, or painful swelling in the parts of their body they use most[38][39]. (Mobel, the archetypal Purity user, had swollen, aching joints and irritated skin from incessant ritual cleaning and channeling of purity energy[38][39].) It is as if the resonance “burns away” impurities within the user as well – including beneficial elements – leaving them physically brittle over time. On a psychological level, the cost is isolation. The more one devotes to Purity, the more one tends to grow severe, uncompromising, and isolated from others. Relationships may fall away as the user’s worldview turns absolutist. Purity users often develop an all-or-nothing mentality that brooks no empathy for mistakes (in themselves or others), which can lead to loneliness and fanaticism. There is also a spiritual warning: some say that absolute purity is akin to emptiness. Push Purity to its limit and you risk erasing so much “impurity” that nothing remains, including your own humanity. Indeed, when Mobel’s powers reached their apex during the Fathom Break, his body combusted in a violent, self-immolating transformation – he became a being of pure, cleaving fire but lost even his name, turning into the fearsome entity “Blemo”[40]. That is Purity’s final cost: to purge everything, even oneself.
Personality & Traits: Purity-aligned individuals tend to be zealous, idealistic, and inflexible. In gentle form, this can mean a devout person with high standards and personal discipline (e.g. a healer who fastidiously sterilizes tools and rituals). In extreme form, it produces fanatics who see the world in black and white. Mobel started as a temple keeper obsessed with cleanliness rituals – a quiet man of faith whose obsession grew in the post-Piercing chaos: if the world was broken and “contaminated” by lattice dust, he felt only absolute purification rituals could restore meaning[30][31]. This anxious fixation is common in Purity practitioners; they often develop OCD-like behaviors, fixating on minute imperfections. They are typically not easygoing people – expect stubbornness, a tendency to judge others harshly, and a kind of righteous impatience. Culturally, no large “Purity faction” arose at first (unlike Form, Wholeness, Entropy which had Structuralists, Continuists, Releasers). Instead, Purity simmered in certain religious sects and among individuals like Mobel. It wasn’t until later that these people coalesced, and when they did, it was as a radical movement rather than an organized guild. People fearful of moral decay or magical pollution found themselves drawn to Purity’s promise of cleansing fire. There is also a personal cost in personality: many Purity users become increasingly ascetic. They give up pleasures (viewed as indulgences that “pollute” the soul), often leading spartan, joyless lives in pursuit of an ever-receding ideal.
Worship & Mythos: The Fathom Break elevated Purity to outright godhood in the form of Blemo, the Purity Incarnate (formerly Mobel). Blemo emerged from a literal baptism by fire – a figure of living flame and judgment, separating “pure from impure” with a mere glance[41]. In the aftermath, radical devotees rallied to Blemo[41]. They saw the apocalyptic destruction that occurred (much of it caused by Purity’s unchecked power) not as tragedy but as a necessary purging of a corrupt world. Thus, Purity gained a cult of worship that espouses extreme doctrine: only those deemed pure (by their new god’s standards) deserve to inherit the new world. Culturally, this has translated into frightening practices – “Scourgers” traveling to burn out pockets of perceived corruption, communities undergoing forced purification rites. Even before Blemo’s rise, the idea of purity had religious connotations (sin and absolution). Now, with a tangible god, Purity theology exploded into something resembling theocracies in areas under Blemo’s influence. The personality of Purity as a deity is uncompromising and wrathful; Blemo is worshiped with both awe and fear as a god who grants salvation through destruction. Some cultures refer to Purity’s divine aspect as “The Cleansing Flame” or “The All-White Light” – interestingly, a light that tolerates no colors (no diversity). In mythic terms, Purity is the promise of paradise if one can eliminate every impurity – a promise that has led many down a fanatical path. Its interplay with Wholeness’s merciful, inclusive goddess (Leesa) forms a dramatic religious dichotomy post-Fathom: compassion vs. judgement.
Wholeness – The Principle of Continuity and Connection (Continuity Resonance)
Essence & Effects: Wholeness (often called Continuity by practitioners) is the resonance of connection, healing, and unity. Its signature is a warm, mid-range frequency that feels like a gentle hum or heartbeat in the air[42]. Wholeness resonators excel at mending and linking: they can heal wounds by knitting tissues together, repair shattered objects by re-establishing their continuity, and even bridge disparate elements (for instance, binding a metal joint to a glass pane seamlessly). The effect is to make something whole again, whether literally (healing a broken bone, closing a rift in a wall) or metaphorically (soothing emotional discord, strengthening community bonds through empathic resonance). Continuity magic often manifests as a copper-gold glow enveloping the target[42] – a visual sign of life and warmth returning. A classic example is Jhace’s first uncontrolled Soulpulse: desperate to save his friend, he unconsciously resonated with her body and the metal trapping her, causing both the metal’s cracks and her head wound to knit closed simultaneously[8][43]. Wholeness can also extend to maintaining energy flow (practitioners used it to stabilize Te’Oga’s failing heat-grid by closing gaps and smoothing the flow of heat currents). Uniquely, Wholeness resonance can create empathic links – a healer might take on a bit of a patient’s pain to relieve them, or link two people’s energies so they bolster each other. In summary, Wholeness is about integration**: making the many function as one.
Metaphysical Role: Wholeness/Continuity stands as the force of unity in the cosmos. It is opposed to Purity’s divisive ethos. Whereas Purity splits and isolates, Wholeness joins and includes. Its divine opposite is Purity, making these two principles a moral dichotomy: compassion vs. zealotry, acceptance vs. exclusion. Wholeness seeks to preserve the web of life; it treats the world’s brokenness by weaving threads back together. It’s also inherently about continuum – seeing past, present, future as a connected flow, and individuals as parts of a greater whole. This principle underpinned the philosophy of the Continuists (hence the name): the idea that knowledge and power should flow freely among people, and that cooperation is strength[44][45]. On a grand scale, one might say Wholeness is what keeps reality “sticking together” – the glue of existence, ensuring that when things fall apart, they can find their way back. It opposes not only Purity but also counters the fragmenting effect of unchecked entropy (though Wholeness ultimately accepts entropy as part of the life-cycle, focusing on meaningful connections until the end).
Costs & Limitations: Wholeness users pay a cost of self-blurring and emotional burden. Because their magic works by connecting themselves to the target (even if metaphorically), they often feel what the target feels. To heal, a Continuity resonator must open themselves up, creating an empathic bridge. This can lead to Identity Bleed – the user’s sense of self can become diffuse, especially after many healings or connections[46]. They might pick up fragments of others’ emotions or memories, or simply lose track of where their needs end and others’ begin[46]. Many Continuity practitioners report that after intense sessions, they have trouble remembering their own desires, feeling instead the echo of those they helped. This is closely linked to what’s known as Sympathetic Overload, a dangerous state where a healer is too attuned to a patient and cannot disengage – essentially being trapped in resonance with the other’s pain[47]. In those cases, the healer might literally experience the injury or trauma of the patient as if it were their own, and require another to break the link[47]. Physically, Wholeness use still causes vein-burn if done improperly, but its unique strain is fatigue. Knitting things together takes energy; Wholeness practitioners often feel drained to the point of exhaustion after heavy use, as if they poured a part of their life force into sustaining someone else. There is also the long-term cost of personal boundaries eroding: Tiffani, who was a gifted Continuity (Wholeness) resonator as well as a Structural resonator, had to teach herself restraint – by N03 she used Soulpulse sparingly because each use exacerbated her chronic pain and hand tremors[48] (partly due to structural cost, partly due to Wholeness overuse causing her to literally feel everyone’s hurt around her, a psychological toll). Thus, Wholeness demands balance: healers must remember to heal themselves and maintain identity, or they “bleed out” emotionally.
Personality & Traits: Those aligned with Wholeness tend to be empathetic, compassionate, and collaborative[42]. They often instinctively seek to help and bring people together. Many were natural medics, caregivers, or community organizers even before discovering their magic. In conflict, they prefer reconciliation to victory. This personality made Wholeness the heart of the largest early faction, the Continuists (“Bleeders”)[44]. Continuists championed open access to knowledge and healing for all, shunning the notion of restricting Soulpulse by licenses or hierarchy[44][45]. They earned the nickname “Bleeders” both because their healing often involved taking on others’ suffering (bleeding themselves) and as a play on their tendency to let resources and help flow freely (bleeding out aid without reservation). What some saw as self-sacrificing virtue, critics saw as lack of boundaries or “bleeding heart” naiveté. Continuity resonators also exhibit a strong sense of community identity – they often find strength in numbers and support networks. A downside in personality can be indecisiveness or enabling behavior: wanting to save everyone, they sometimes struggle to make hard choices (for example, a Wholeness user might exhaust themselves trying to save multiple wounded instead of prioritizing, potentially saving none). Still, their presence is literally life-saving. It was noted that in any large settlement, the Continuity-affined naturally gravitated to roles like nurses, mediators, or teachers, knitting society together post-catastrophe.
Worship & Mythos: The apotheosis of Wholeness came in the form of Leesa, Goddess of Wholeness (born from Salee). During the Confluence/Fathom event, Salee, a healer, absorbed a massive wave of others’ pain and in doing so transcended – she became a living avatar of mercy, instantly healing dozens around her[49][50]. Revered as a Goddess of Compassion, Leesa’s emergence turned the Continuist ethic into a literal religion. Worshipers of Leesa see her as the embodiment of the Motherly Principle: all are connected in her embrace. Temples to Leesa emphasize communal care, and her followers (sometimes called Healers or Mercykin) travel to war-torn or plague-ridden areas to perform miraculous healings in her name. Under Leesa’s influence, the ideology of Wholeness sharpened: mercy is paramount, even to one’s own detriment. Ethically, this has raised dilemmas – some Leesa devotees take a vow to take on the suffering of others, which can become problematic if done recklessly. Theologically, Wholeness is seen as the divine light of unity, the promise that “all broken things shall be made whole.” It is a comforting doctrine in a shattered world. However, even among her faithful, there is a cautionary tale: Leesa’s own transformation required enormous sacrifice (she literally had to embrace the suffering of countless dying to ascend). Thus, priests of Wholeness teach balance and consent – one should not force healing where it’s refused, and one must not martyr oneself to the point of “hollowing out,” as even compassion has limits. In contrast to Blemo’s harsh puritanism, Leesa’s creed is one of unconditional love – making their factions natural enemies in the post-Fathom era.
Entropy – The Principle of Dissolution and Endings (Dissolution Resonance)
Essence & Effects: Entropy (often termed Dissolution resonance) governs decay, release, and the gentle ushering of endings. Its frequency is low, soft, and fading, often likened to a deep sigh or the final note of a song trailing off[51]. Entropy resonators can accelerate decay in materials (rust iron to brittle flakes in seconds, cause plants to wither or fruit to rot at a touch), dissolve bonds (undo mortar between bricks, weaken barriers), and ease transitions (most notably, easing the dying in their final moments or calming severe pain by encouraging the body to let go). Unlike Purity’s destructive flame, Entropy’s touch is quiet and often invisible – things simply fall apart, usually peacefully. In a controlled context, Dissolution can be incredibly useful: disposing of waste safely, composting dead matter into fertile soil rapidly, or dismantling damaged structures without explosives. On a battlefield or conflict scenario, Entropy magic might manifest as ghostly gray energy that causes enemy weapons to corrode and crumble mid-swing, or induces exhaustion and surrender in foes by making them acutely feel the weight of all things ending. It’s notably effective at dispelling other magical constructs – an entropy pulse can unravel a Form resonance structure or nullify ongoing spells by encouraging them to conclude. A hallmark story of Entropy resonance is of Eries, a novitiate fascinated with death: she possessed the calm ability to crystallize and shatter flora around her in moments of stress, essentially speeding their life cycle to a beautiful end[52][53]. Her perspective – “what was solid becomes soft, what resisted yields” – perfectly encapsulates Entropy’s ethos[54][55].
Metaphysical Role: Entropy is the end of the cycle, the force that ensures nothing is permanent so that new beginnings can occur. It is not malicious destruction but completion. Its divine opposite is Form – order and permanence vs. impermanence and release. When Form builds a towering edifice, Entropy is the patience that eventually wears it down. Importantly, Entropy in this magical context carries a nuance of acceptance. It aligns with philosophies that embrace death as natural and see decay as necessary for renewal (the fallen leaves nourishing new growth). Among the four principles, Entropy is the one most closely tied to time and the natural lifecycle. Practitioners often speak of “the Fading” – the moment of ending – as something sacred. In Te’Oga’s cultural landscape, this principle was openly revered by the Releaser faction (the “Enders”) even before any godhood manifested[56]. Releasers believed in making endings gentle and purposeful, whether that meant euthanizing someone beyond saving or letting a crumbling structure collapse in a controlled way rather than forcing it to stand. Entropy ensures that struggle ceases and peace follows, as one sacred text described[54][57].
Costs & Limitations: For those who channel Entropy, the primary cost is vitality and motivation. They give a bit of their own life energy to fuel the hastening of decay (or they align with the ambient decay energy, which is a cold, draining force). After significant use, Dissolution resonators report feeling profound fatigue, melancholy, and a sense of emptiness[51]. It’s as if in ending other things, they themselves inch closer to an ending. Many Entropy practitioners struggle with depression or apathy: connecting deeply with the principle of “everything ends” can sap one’s drive to begin or sustain anything. Physical signs of overuse include premature aging (some heavy users found streaks of gray hair or persistent weariness in youth) and a certain chill in the limbs – their circulatory system metaphorically slows. They can also experience moments of dissociation, a symptom of their identity loosening much like Wholeness users, but for a different reason: rather than blending with others, they detach from everything. In extreme cases, an Entropy user might become frighteningly emotionless or passive, having accepted fate to a harmful degree. Another limitation is that Entropy cannot be selective once set in motion. If not carefully directed, a dissolution effect might spread beyond its intended target (rot doesn’t stop easily). Thus, finesse is needed to avoid collateral decay. For example, dissolving the bonds of one stone in a wall, if done sloppily, could propagate weakness to adjacent stones – a skilled Dissolution resonator learns to “pluck just the one thread” rather than unravel the whole tapestry at once. Overconfidence or carelessness can result in over-dissolution – a scenario where more ends than the user intended, which can be disastrous if, say, you only meant to wither enemy crops but end up blighting your own fields as well. Therefore, many Entropy practitioners adopt a careful, measured approach by necessity (which suits their temperament).
Personality & Traits: Those attuned to Entropy tend to be calm, accepting, and often introspective[57][58]. They are the types who are comfortable with solitude and have made peace with loss. In the immediate aftermath of the Piercing, many who resonated with Entropy became hospice workers, undertakers, or counselors for the grieving – roles that fit their natural inclination to provide comfort at the end. They are sometimes seen as morbid or overly pessimistic by others, but in truth many Dissolution resonators are gentle souls who simply view death and decay as truths rather than tragedies. The Releasers (Enders) faction embodied this, operating in burial grounds and quarantine zones, wearing ash-gray veils and performing quiet rites[56]. Their motto could be “All things, in time.” Personality-wise, they may come off as detached or fatalistic (“what will be, will be”). However, their detachment gives them grace under pressure – while others panic, an Entropy adept remains composed, doing what must be done even if it means triaging or letting go of something precious. They also often have a wry sense of humor about life’s transience. One notable trait is empathy through witnessing (as opposed to Wholeness’s empathy through sharing) – they won’t absorb your pain, but they will sit with you through it unflinchingly. Some can be overly passive, failing to act until it’s too late, because they assume the natural course should not be altered. This was a criticism leveled at figures like Venn, a Dissolution master who led the Releasers: he believed in minimal intervention, which was merciful in some cases but perceived as cold neglect in others.
Worship & Mythos: In the wake of Fathom Break, Entropy’s pure incarnation appeared as Seeri (once Eries). Seeri became a kind of goddess of peaceful endings and enlightenment[52][59]. Her transformation was marked not by fire or explosion, but by a serene dissolution: nearby flora crystallized and shattered beautifully as she herself transcended, leaving her with an aura of calm finality[52][59]. Wanderers and common folk who saw this proclaimed her enlightenment, akin to a Buddha of entropy[60]. Seeri’s worshipers are often philosophers, nomads, or those traumatized by the endless struggles – they seek solace in Seeri’s message that ending is not to be feared. As a deity, Seeri doesn’t command large militant orders but rather a diffuse following of philosophers and sages. It’s noted that about a year after the Break, a faction of “Philosophers” had emerged, likely those who follow Entropy’s contemplative approach[61]. They preach that the Era of Gods is a natural evolution and that clinging to the old world only brings suffering. Their ethics emphasize mercy-killing to end suffering and the dissolution of corrupt institutions to allow rebirth. In art, Seeri is depicted as a figure of glass and petals drifting away, embodying beauty in transience. Her rise turned many Releasers’ practices into religious sacraments: funerals became holy send-offs with resonance rituals guiding souls to rest, and even daily chores like composting got spiritual significance. The mythology around Entropy thus reinforces the idea that in every end, there is peace. Still, Seeri’s followers can be radical in their own quiet way: a subset called “The Yielded” believe in hastening the end of the age of human toil entirely, essentially welcoming apocalypse as the ultimate act of mercy and renewal. This demonstrates that even a principle about acceptance has its dogma when deified.
Soulpulse Progression Across the Five Phases (N01–N05)
Over the course of the five novellas of The Confluence Chronicles, the understanding and application of Soulpulse magic evolved dramatically. Each narrative phase – Ember, Shaping, Alloy, Prism, Confluence/Fathom – corresponds to a stage in the magic system’s development, from rudimentary spark to world-altering crescendo. Below is a breakdown of how Soulpulse progresses through these phases:
Ember Phase – Awakening the Spark (Novella 1, “Ember”)
The Ember Phase represents the ignition of Soulpulse in the world. In the immediate aftermath of the Piercing (a cataclysmic event where a massive projectile pierced Te’Oga, wreaking havoc[4][1]), magic first flared in desperate responses to disaster. People didn’t yet know what Soulpulse was – it was a mysterious power awakened by crisis, an ember of hope in the ruins. Key developments and characteristics of this phase:
*         
First         Sparks of Magic: Soulpulse usage was inadvertent and         instinctual. The classic example is Jhace in the ruins of a         collapsed district: with no training, he somehow caused debris to         shift and a grievous wound to heal when trying to save his         sister-figure Chloen[8][43].         He had no name for what he did, only the result – a life saved and         his own arms scorched by unseen energy. Similarly, others across         Te’Oga experienced small miracles or weird occurrences as they         struggled to survive (a child’s cry causing shattered glass to         reassemble around them, a panicked smith accidentally fusing a         broken pipe shut by yelling at it, etc.). These events were isolated         embers in the dark, hinting at a new force.
*         
Catastrophe         and Necessity: The Piercing left the world literally tilted (the         planet’s axis realigned) and infrastructure in ruins[62][1].         Out of necessity, survivors began cooperating across old guild         lines. Former rival crafters – the forge-smiths and glass-smiths –         had to combine their knowledge to stabilize buildings and the vital         heat-grid that kept cities warm[63][64].         In this pressure cooker of necessity, Soulpulse was frequently         triggered by strong emotions: fear, love, determination. It was         unreliable – a phenomenon that “just happened” when         people reached emotional peaks – but those early successes (and         failures) planted the seed that something beyond tools was at         work.
*         
The         Piercing’s Magical Aftermath: The environment itself was         altered. Most notably, the Piercing created Lattice Dust, a         fine glittering dust that fell like ash everywhere and coated         everything with a faint hum[65].         This dust, a byproduct of whatever energy was unleashed, became a         permanent feature and early on was just a nuisance and health hazard         (it irritated lungs and corroded metals)[66].         But crucially, its presence hinted that the world had been         “suffused” with a new resonance – the dust literally hummed         with faint magical vibration[65].         In Ember phase, people didn’t know what to do about it, but some         observant characters (like Tiffani) noted that the dust tended to         gather or respond when Soulpulse was used, almost like iron filings         around a magnet. Thus, the dust served as a visible marker of the         invisible: magic was now in the very air and ash.
*         
Learning         Through Crisis: The Ember phase was characterized by trial by         fire. There were many mishaps: a person might desperately try to         replicate a Soulpulse feat and end up with severe vein-burn or         collapsing from a vein-snap, not understanding the limitations. Each         time, though, small lessons were learned. For instance, after         Jhace’s arms were vein-burned, Tiffani observed the glowing         pattern in his veins and realized this energy traveled through         specific channels – she later cautioned him to “manage that         cost”[67][68],         one of the first acknowledgments that using this power has lasting         consequences. In another instance, a group of survivors attempted a         communal effort to lift rubble by all pushing with their will –         the resulting dissonance knocked everyone flat and caused a minor         quake. From failure, they learned that too many at once without         coordination made things worse. Essentially, Ember was chaotic;         knowledge was sparse and empirical. Yet by the end of Novella 1, the         protagonists had a glimmer of understanding: they knew Soulpulse was         real, repeatable (if still mysterious), and that cooperation and         careful technique seemed key to wielding it safely. The novella ends         on a hopeful note: a partially stabilized heat-grid hums with         a new kind of energy and the survivors share a sense that they have         discovered the “spark that will hold their world together”[69].         The metaphor of an ember is apt – small and fragile, but with         potential to grow into something powerful if properly stoked.
Shaping Phase – First Understanding and Systematization (Novella 2, “Shaping”)
In the Shaping Phase, the characters move from mere survival to curiosity and experimentation, attempting to shape a coherent system out of the chaos. This is when Soulpulse began to be studied, named, and taught (albeit informally). Key features of this phase:
   *         
Discovery         of Resonance Theory: The breakthrough comes when Tiffani and         other thinkers conduct deliberate experiments on Soulpulse         phenomena. They identify that it’s all about vibration and         frequency matching, essentially formulating the core principle:         Soulpulse is sympathetic resonance magic, not brute force[15].         They observe that success comes when the user seems “in tune”         with the material (e.g., humming at a certain pitch while working         made things easier) and failure comes with discord. This is         articulated clearly for the first time: “You can’t force         something to change; you have to resonate with it until it wants to         change.”[15]         This understanding marks the true birth of Soulpulse as a knowable         system. Terminology emerges: they speak of “finding the right         frequency” of a task, of achieving “resonance”         versus creating “dissonance”, and of “attunement”         as the process to get there[70][7].         Essentially, the Shaping phase is about learning the rules.
   *         
Lexicon         Expansion: A whole new vocabulary is coined as         trial-and-error results are discussed among practitioners[71][7].         Some key terms defined during this phase:
   *         
Frequency/Resonance: The unique         vibration of person or object[72].
   *         
Harmonic: When two people’s pulses         align naturally, allowing synergistic teamwork[9]         (rare, but now understood as something to strive for in paired         efforts).
   *         
Dissonance: The identified word for         the painful clash that had hurt so many; now people knew to avoid         “causing dissonance” by mismatched attempts[7].
   *         
Attuning: The method of gradually         adjusting one’s output to sync with the target[11].
   *         
Vein-burn: They name the internal         injuries, realizing it’s a direct consequence of dissonance (like         friction burn in the magical veins)[43][6].
   *         
Vein-Echo:         Discovered when practitioners noted a “ringing” in their senses         after using Soulpulse; they learned not to spam their power because         the echo needed to fade[23].         Each term gave practitioners power over the phenomenon through         understanding. By naming it, they could teach it and avoid pitfalls         more systematically.
   *         
Catastrophic         Failures and Lessons: The Shaping phase still saw plenty of         accidents – in fact, the drive to experiment meant new         types of failures occurred. Some notable ones:
   *         
Vein-Snap incidents became         well-documented; people learned how far they could push their         internal channels. If someone collapsed coughing blood, it was         recognized as vein-snap and not a mysterious illness, prompting         protocols like enforced rest for those individuals[25].
   *         
Resonance Cascade became a feared term         after an incident where an out-of-tune pulse triggered a chain         reaction that brought down an entire half-repaired building[10].         This taught them that large-scale Soulpulse work had to be planned         with failsafes (e.g. smaller contained pulses rather than one         massive blast, or using damping materials around).
   *         
Sympathetic         Overload was first observed directly during this phase: a healer         attuning to a grievously injured patient started screaming in agony         as if the injuries were hers[47].         Only when another practitioner jarred her with a forceful shove         (breaking her concentration) did she snap out. This led to the         practice of partner oversight – whenever someone attempted         deep healing, a second person would monitor and be ready to break         the connection if needed[47].         These failures were shared in emerging scholarly notes (the closest         thing to academia at that time, mostly letters between guild members         and open discussions in relief camps).
   *         
Factions         Forming – Affinity Realization: As more people experimented,         it became clear that individuals had affinities for certain         kinds of effects[73][28].         This was the era when, thanks to Tiffani’s “resonance mapping         method”, people lined up to test which frequency felt most natural         to them[74][75].         The discovery: roughly three major types (plus hints of a fourth)         emerged:
   *         
Structural Resonators (Form-aligned) –         those whose energy ran high and sharp, excellent at reinforcing and         structuring[28].
   *         
Continuity Resonators (Wholeness-aligned) –         those with warm, midrange energy ideal for mending and         connecting[42].
   *         
Dissolution Resonators (Entropy-aligned) –         those with low, soft energy attuned to decay and gentle endings[51].
   *         
Purity         – at this stage, Purity was not officially recognized as a         separate affinity by the general populace; however, there were “odd         ones” who didn’t cleanly fit the three and exhibited signs of         something else (e.g. an unusually intense, narrow resonance that         didn’t mend or simply decay, but burned selectively). Only         later would they realize these were Purity attuned individuals.         During Shaping, such people might have been lumped in with         Structuralists or seen as aberrant. Mobel’s early increasingly         strict purification rituals (from N01’s interlude through N02)         were a case in point: he had a resonance that aggravated his body         (swollen joints) and seemed to do nothing except cause pain         unless channeled into cleansing acts[38][31].         Those like him were outliers who didn’t yet form a public group.         As people identified their affinities, the old guild system         (forge vs. glass) indeed fractured entirely[76][73].         New alliances formed around these resonance types, because a         structural resonator smith might find more common ground with a         structural resonator architect than with a non-resonant smith. By         the end of Shaping phase, the seeds of the later factions         (Structuralists, Continuists, Releasers) were firmly planted, even         if formal faction names were only just emerging[77][78].
   *         
Cultural         Shifts: With knowledge spreading, Soulpulse began to be seen not         as miraculous anomaly but as a craft in its own right.         Populace attitudes shifted from fear to a mix of awe and normalizing         curiosity. There were public demonstrations – Tiffani’s         organized testing events attracted hundreds[74][79].         For many common folk, witnessing Soulpulse use went from “terrifying         display” to “useful service” during this phase. Also, the         economics started shifting: those with useful resonance skills         became in high demand for reconstruction work. The Shaping phase         ends with a sense of structured learning – a small academy         of thought forming even if not literally in a school. By now the         world has the basic grammar of the magic, setting the stage for more         advanced uses and, unfortunately, conflicts over how it should be         used.
Alloy Phase – Conflict, Fusion, and Limits Tested (Novella 3, “Alloy”)
The Alloy Phase is where multiple elements – knowledge, factions, personal ideologies – fuse and clash. Just as an alloy is a mixture of metals forged in fire, this stage sees the forging of alliances and the eruption of conflicts that test the limits of the magic system and its users. Key aspects include:
      *         
Factional Solidification and Clash:         What was seeded in Shaping blooms (or festers) in Alloy. The three         main affinity-based factions fully form:
      *         
Structuralists (Form-aligned) entrench         their power, advocating strict regulation of Soulpulse use “for         the greater good of order.” They begin enforcing Resonance         Licensing in their territories[34]         – anyone practicing magic must be certified, echoing their ethos         of control and fear of chaos. They see Soulpulse as something that         must be governed like any dangerous resource.
      *         
Continuists (Wholeness-aligned)         coalesce into a loose network championing open sharing and mutual         aid, resisting any regulation[45].         They are disorganized by nature (preferring consensus over         hierarchy) but very numerous, acting as healers and community         supporters wherever they go.
      *         
Releasers (Entropy-aligned) remain         smaller and more philosophically detached, but by now recognized as         vital – they handle burials, disease containment, and mercy         killings when needed, all with solemn respect[56].         They often stay neutral or mediate between the other two, though         their fatalism sometimes puts them at odds with both.
      *         
Purity-aligned individuals still don’t         have a named faction, but their presence is felt in rising extremist         rhetoric especially within certain Structuralist offshoots or         religious circles. Some Structuralists who were particularly zealous         about “cleaning up” misuse or “removing” unlicensed mages         might actually be Purity-inclined without knowing it. They would         later break off, but in Alloy they mostly operate as hardliners         within other groups.
These factions begin territorial disputes[80]. For example, Structuralist enforcers (often referred to by others as “bluecoats” or derisively as “Locksteppers”) might arrest a Continuist healer for unauthorized practice, leading to skirmishes. A Continuist safehouse offering free magical mending might be attacked by extremists who blame uncontrolled magic for accidents. Novella 3’s events show a tragic escalation: a secret cross-faction meeting aimed at peace (organized by an idealistic multi-resonant youth, Chloen) ends in a massacre by Structuralist extremists, fearing that uncontrolled collaboration would threaten their order[81][82]. Chloen’s death in that massacre is an emotional turning point – it brutally demonstrates how far apart the factions have drifted and that neutrality is becoming impossible[83][84]. In Alloy phase, conflict pushes Soulpulse usage to new contexts: espionage (sensing spies via pulse-sense), sabotage (Structuralists use Form resonance to covertly weaken structures in Continuist zones and frame them as accidents[85]), and open street battles where magic is weaponized in improvised ways.
         *         
Personal         Fusion of Techniques: On the more positive side, “Alloy”         also symbolizes integration of methods. Characters like Jhace         and Tiffani truly combine their forge and glass guild teachings into         a unified approach to Soulpulse. By now, Jhace has learned         patience and precision, and Tiffani has learned to trust intuition         at times – together they develop dual-craft techniques that         revolutionize repair work[86][14].         They effectively create an alloy of methodologies, showing         others that synergy yields better results than rivalry. This         influences many on the ground: e.g., Kylar, a smith who was         initially a stubborn Structuralist, witnesses the success of         combined techniques and “stops competing, starts         collaborating”, joining their efforts[87][88].         This shows that even amid factional conflict, at the individual         level there is hope for fusion and understanding – a recurring         theme.
         *         
Pushing the         Limits of Capacity: Alloy phase brings the first instances of         people deliberately trying to exceed known limits – often         with dire consequences – thus revealing where the hard boundaries         lie.
         *         
Multi-resonance attempts: We see or         hear of more individuals who, like Jhace, might have the potential         for more than one resonance. Chloen, who was multi-resonant,         tragically dies early, but her existence proves it’s possible to         have breadth. Tiffani, by the end of this phase, hints at her own         hidden dual affinity (though she doesn’t yet openly reveal it).         The idea of combining principles is no longer unthinkable; some         scholars begin theorizing about harmonics, though it’s more an         academic question at this stage.
         *         
Overuse and Hollowing: With conflicts         raging, some practitioners start overusing their powers         severely. We hear of frontline healers who attend to wounded for         days without rest, Structuralist taskmasters forcing teams to lift         entire buildings in one go – and then the fallout. Hollowing         cases appear: the term coined for those who have essentially “burned         out” their Soulpulse completely[89].         They end up in a catatonic state, veins inert, eyes vacant,         resonance dead inside them – a fate worse than normal exhaustion         because it’s permanent[89].         Alloy phase provides the first confirmed hollows. It’s a grim         warning that there are no infinite batteries; one’s conviction and         spirit can be shattered by overextension. Notably, Jhace         himself becomes so fearful of the sympathetic overload incident and         of causing harm that in N03 (Alloy) he uses Soulpulse very         sparingly[90][91],         indicating a growing awareness of personal limit.
         *         
Emotional         Toll and Ethics: The heavy events of Alloy push characters into         questioning the ethics of Soulpulse use. For instance, after         Chloen’s death, Tiffani and Jhace both conclude that standing         aside (neutral) is no longer viable – not using their gifts         can enable tragedy[92][81].         This is a maturation in understanding: the magic system isn’t just         a neutral tool; how it’s used or not used has moral weight. They         realize Soulpulse has socio-political consequences and thus users         must take responsibility for those. This introspection sets the         stage for more structured principles or “laws” of responsible         use later.
         *         
Technology         and Soulpulse Fusion: By the end of Alloy, we see the beginnings         of Soul-tech integration. For example, some engineers among         the Structuralists devise resonance-based alarm systems (crystal         sensors that ring when unauthorized pulses occur). The idea of a         device that could suppress or detect Soulpulse is floated         (foreshadowing the suppression tech in the next phase). Meanwhile,         Continuists experiment with healing gadgets, like lattice-dust         salves that vibrate to promote healing when activated by a user’s         pulse. These are prototypes, but they mark the start of a         forge-punk/glass-punk spin on the magic: physical devices augmenting         or channeling resonance.
The Alloy phase thus is one of tension and combination – the world is figuratively alloying disparate elements (for good and ill). It ends on a somber note with guilds collapsed into warring factions and the main characters steeling themselves to intervene more directly in these conflicts, acknowledging that the system they helped shape is being used to both heal and harm. It’s the calm before an even bigger storm, as all sides prepare for the trials of the next stage.
Prism Phase – Refinement, Extremes, and Breaking Points (Novella 4, “Prism”)
The Prism Phase, named for the idea of a prism splitting light into distinct colors, is characterized by specialization, clarity, and also fragmentation. Here the four principles and their practitioners reach new heights and extremes, as if the earlier “alloy” has now been split into its pure components under pressure. Major elements of this stage:
            *         
Peak         Specialization & The Visionary Project: In this phase, each         faction doubles down on its ideals, yielding remarkable advancements         and dire consequences. The Structuralists under Master Corlexi         (dubbed “The Visionary”) embark on an ambitious project in the         city of Prism: constructing a massive geometric glass tower         meant to be a testament to Form resonance – perfect angles,         flawless structure, built by hundreds of resonators working in         unison[93][94].         This is Form taken to an extreme ideal. The project pushes         Structural resonators beyond safe limits in pursuit of perfection.         It ends in catastrophe: two top apprentices Hollow mid-ritual,         unable to sustain the intense constant resonance, and the partially         raised tower collapses spectacularly[94][95].         Corlexi himself begins to Hollow as well – essentially a breakdown         of the most gifted Form user under the weight of his own impossible         goal[95].         The Visionary’s Grand Project serves as a caution: it shows         that even with all their knowledge, the practitioners are not         immune to hubris. It also illustrates the concept of         god-compulsion emerging – Corlexi was driven by an almost         superhuman obsession as if the principle of Form itself was         overtaking his human limits[96].
            *         
Emergence         of Dual-Principle Masters: Prism phase is when the secret about         dual resonance finally comes to light. Tiffani, who had been         trained by an unknown mentor pre-Piercing, reveals in a critical         moment that she can deliberately wield two principles at once         (Form and Wholeness)[97][98].         She does this to save Jhace from near death by healing him with         Wholeness while structurally reinforcing his failing body with         Form[99][17].         This revelation astonishes those around her – until then, Jhace’s         occasional multi-principle flairs were chalked up to unique         instinct, and formal doctrine held that one person could not channel         two resonances simultaneously. Tiffani’s act proves multi-affinity         can be a trained skill, not just a fluke[100].         It hints at deeper knowledge (her mysterious mentor clearly knew         more about Soulpulse than most). This development is pivotal because         it cracks open the door for broader thinking: if two principles are         possible in one person, what about three or all four? It sets the         stage for the concept of Confluence. Culturally, Tiffani’s         dual mastery remains rare – by the end of Prism phase, she’s         perhaps the only one openly doing it – but it plants seeds of both         hope (maybe unified use can solve problems) and fear (mixing powers         could be dangerously uncharted, akin to playing god).
            *         
Worsening         Hollowing & Conviction Crisis: With multiple incidents of         overextension (the Visionary’s collapse, war skirmishes, etc.),         Hollowing becomes a recognized epidemic in Prism         phase[93][95].         Many who pushed past their limits are now incurably hollow, which         has a chilling effect on the community. Practitioners realize there         is a point of no return. This forces a philosophical crisis:         Hollowing isn’t just physical exhaustion; it’s described as         “when a user’s conviction fails catastrophically”, a         soul-level burnout[89].         So factions start placing more emphasis on mental training, belief         systems, or anything to keep conviction strong. For example:
            *         
Structuralist leadership doubles down on         ideology of order to keep their members’ conviction high         (convincing them that their cause of perfection is worth any cost,         so they won’t mentally break).
            *         
Continuists preach self-care and taking         shifts to avoid anyone losing themselves entirely – their open,         collaborative approach actually gives them resilience, as burden is         shared.
            *         
Releasers accept Hollowing almost as a         natural thing for those who resist ends; they take in some Hollows         into care, though they can’t cure them.
            *         
A subplot in         Novella 4 involves investigating the Hollowing cases, confirming         they are irreversible and not a disease that can be cured by healing         – this underscores that it’s a limit of the magic itself,         not just an injury[97][98].
            *         
Anti-Soulpulse         Technology – The Sanitists: Prism phase sees the rise of those         who fear or resent the chaos magic has brought. Referred to as         Sanitists (a movement or perhaps a government-backed group),         they begin developing suppression technology to control or         nullify Soulpulse[101][102].         Hints of this tech appear – devices that emit a dissonant field or         use some property of lattice dust to “jam” resonance. By the end         of N04, this technology is nearly ready (Chekhov’s gun for N05).         In story, perhaps the protagonists become aware that certain areas         dampen their powers slightly, or they find schematics for a device         that could globally silence the veins. This is the mundane world’s         response to the extraordinary: a very forge-punk solution of         “build a machine to tame the magic.” It represents the         crystallization of non-practitioner fear and the potential for an         external check on magic-users.
            *         
Emotional         and Social Prism: True to the name “Prism,” this phase         refracts the cast of characters emotionally. Each main character         faces their personal truth under pressure:
            *         
Jhace nearly dies from pushing himself         (Hollowing almost claims him) and through that humbling experience,         he learns to respect limits and interdependence[103][104].         By the finale of N04 he has grown, finding a sustainable way to use         his powers (even discovering a minor self-healing technique for his         lingering injuries)[103][105].
            *         
Tiffani reveals more of her secret knowledge         and must confront the burden of it – she partially confesses to         Jhace that she had special training, bridging some of the trust         gap[17][106].         She faces guilt for not sharing everything and the physical toll of         dual-use (her vein-burn scar on her arm grows from 3.5 cm to 4.2 cm,         a small detail indicating the cost of her saving Jhace[107][108]).         Emotionally she’s relieved that Jhace still trusts her despite         mysteries[98][109].
            *         
Corlexi (Visionary) essentially becomes a         fallen idol – his collapse shatters the myth that one         principle (Form) alone can save Te’Oga. His followers are         disillusioned or frightened, and some interpret his catatonic state         as a sign that something bigger is trying to birth through         him (which foreshadows his eventual transformation in N05).
            *         
Mobel (Purity zealot) in this phase likely         goes from quiet to radical. By now he’s probably split from the         Structuralists after seeing them as too compromising, and has         gathered a small cult of like-minded purificationists. Possibly an         event like him confronting a corrupt official and “cleansing”         them publicly happens, marking Purity’s violent emergence. The         Prism theme of fragmentation is at play: Purity splits off into its         own open movement by the end of this stage, even if smaller than         others.
Overall, Prism phase is about clarity through division. Each color of the magic spectrum now shines separately: the world sees what pure Form obsession leads to, what pure Mercy can do, how pure Purity manifests, etc. It’s beautiful in achievements (the tower lifting, dual magic healing) but also deadly (the tower collapse, hollowings, fanatic violence). By conclusion of Novella 4, the world has stabilized its infrastructure (~90% grid restored[110]) but at the cost of stability in other areas: political and spiritual tensions are at a breaking point. Everyone is bracing for an impending showdown of ideologies and powers, which arrives in the final phase.
Confluence/Fathom Phase – The Ultimate Union and the Breaking of Reality (Novella 5, “Confluence”, culminating in the Fathom Break)
The final phase brings everything to a head. Confluence refers to the combining of all four principles, and the Fathom Break is the apocalyptic event that results from that unprecedented resonance overload. Key developments:
               *         
All-Out Conflict and Weaponization: At         the start of this phase, open war erupts between factions         (particularly the authoritarian Purity faction and an alliance of         Continuists & remaining Structuralist moderates led by Jhace and         Tiffani). Soulpulse is now fully weaponized on the battlefield:
               *         
Purity warriors under Mobel (now openly         declaring only the “Pure” shall rule) use blinding white Purity         flames that burn living and non-living matter deemed         impure[111][112].         They employ horrifying tactics like extracting impurities from         opponents (which in practice can rip out vital essences or cause         internal hemorrhage)[37].
               *         
Continuity healers and Wholeness fighters         form protective choirs, linking their energies to shield         comrades from dissonance and rapidly heal injuries in the middle of         combat[113][16].         This is the first large-scale use of group harmonic resonance in         combat, and it proves effective but taxing.
               *         
Form resonators raise fortifications on the         fly – walls of earth or crystal summoned to block attacks[114].         Jhace himself cycles through multiple principles rapidly: shielding         allies with Wholeness, raising barriers with Form, nullifying a         poison gas with Purity, and destabilizing an enemy siege engine with         Entropy in quick succession[113][16].         This adaptability astonishes those around him, showing a hint of         Confluence potential even before it fully manifests.
               *         
Entropy users in combat act as saboteurs and         sappers: making enemy weapons brittle, sapping enemy morale (some         Entropy adepts learned to project a sense of despair onto foes, an         emotional resonance attack). They also mercifully take dying         soldiers out of suffering when needed, an understated but crucial         role.
               *         
Pulse-sense         and Tethering: By now, elite fighters developed the skill to         sense opponents’ resonance – essentially a sixth sense of         where and what type of magic the enemy is about to use, by feeling         the vibrations in the air. Duels become mind-games of feints and         frequency shifts. The concept of tethering emerges strongly:         some combatants learn to “tether” onto an enemy’s pulse,         either to disrupt it or to ride it. For instance, a Wholeness         fighter might latch onto a Purity user’s frequency briefly to         soften the impact of their next blast (a risky maneuver akin to         catching a wave at its peak). Conversely, Purity users might tether         to an opponent to inject a burst of dissonance directly, effectively         stealing their resonance momentarily and leaving the target         powerless. The battlefield becomes a web of these unseen tethers and         clashing fields.
               *         
Suppression         Device and the Fathom Break: The critical turning point is the         activation of the Sanitist Suppression Device[115][116].         This device, deployed by anti-magic authorities who fear the         escalating war, is meant to dampen all Soulpulse activity         within a large radius and “steal the fire” from the combatants.         However, its functioning is fundamentally flawed – it blankets the         area (and perhaps the planetary vein network) in a dissonant         counter-frequency. Instead of calming the conflict, it triggers the         nightmare scenario: “Steal Breaks Open.” This is a         catastrophic chain reaction where the suppression field causes the         planetary veins to rupture under pressure[117][118].         All the built-up resonance (from months of heavy use and the current         battle) that was meant to be dampened is suddenly unleashed in one         colossal wave. Reality itself destabilizes: the ground quakes         stop (like an eerie silence before a bigger storm)[119][120],         then a massive multi-colored omni-resonant shockwave erupts         from the ground and sky as the energy escapes every         conduit[21][121].
Simultaneously, in that moment, Jhace experiences ultimate loss – Tiffani sacrifices herself to save him from falling debris, dying in his arms[122][123]. His grief and love unlock something unprecedented: Confluence. Jhace’s soul, in agony, grabs onto all four principles at once instinctively and he unleashes a four-principle Soulpulse outburst[20][21]. This human Confluence merges with the wild surge triggered by the device failure, creating the event known as Fathom Break. The term has multiple meanings: it “breaks” the fathomable limits of magic (going beyond what anyone thought possible), it occurs deep in the “fathoms” of the world’s energy, and it literally breaks the world to some extent.
The effects are mythic and apocalyptic: a blinding pillar of energy punches into the sky[124]; all four colors of resonance intertwine in the blast (gold, blue, white, gray) – witnesses later describe it as if the song of creation itself roared out in discord then harmony. The shockwave travels through the veins of Te’Oga, awakening latent resonance everywhere at once. The immediate battlefield is leveled, but more remarkably, the shockwave triggers distant, simultaneous transformations: - Corlexi, recovering from his earlier Hollowing in a distant city, is hit by the wave of Confluence. The dormant potential in him (Form) is catalyzed and he transforms into Xilcore, the god-form of Structure[125][35]. - Salee (Leesa), Mobel (Blemo), and Eries (Seeri) undergo their respective god-ascensions at that exact moment as well[50][40][59]. Four human vessels, each aligned to one principle, simultaneously absorb the tsunami of resonance and become something more than human. This is the Confluence of all principles in the world, distributed into four focal points. No human had ever wielded all four at once until Jhace’s grief-driven burst, and that act literally created gods by giving those who embodied each principle an infinite charge of their resonance.
Meanwhile, physically, the world cracks: the extreme energy breaks off a chunk of the planet’s crust, levitating a whole region into the air[126]. The phenomenon of gravity faltering and land floating is entirely new – reality’s rules bent by omni-resonance. It causes mass destruction: cities are devastated by quakes ending abruptly then pieces of land flying up; thousands die in the chaos[126][127]. This is the disastrous price of the Fathom Break. In essence, it was as if the resonance field of the entire planet “rang” at full volume, then shattered like glass from the strain.
